DANSKE Bank said it expects to write down around nine billion Danish crowns (1.2bn) of the value of its businesses in Finland, Northern Ireland and Estonia.

Denmark's largest bank by market capitalisation has had to cut staff and branches to recover from the financial cri-sis, when it was hit hard by its exposure to Ireland and weakness in Finland, which has been weighed down by Europe's standoff with Russia.

Shareholders' equity will be reduced by the same amount. The impairments are technical and don't affect strategy, it said.

HD Lithuanian cos hurt by weak ruble - Danske Bank analyst
WC 225 words
PD 16 December 2014
ET 10:20
SN Baltic Business Daily
SC BALDAI
LA English
CY (c) 2014 Baltic News Service

LP 

VILNIUS, Dec 16, BNS - The ruble's slide is painful to Lithuanian companies that generate revenues in the Russian currency, a Danske Bank analyst said.

"The impact (on Lithuanian businesses) is unambiguously negative. The ruble's fall has been dramatic lately. Lithuanian business companies are watching these developments and the ruble's depreciation is painful to them," Giedre Geciauskiene, head of financial markets at Danske Bank Lithuania, told BNS.

TD 

Lithuanian companies generating revenues in rubles will be the most affected, the analyst said.

"If a company has both expenses and revenues in rubles, then, de facto, it experiences no interest risk. However, this is more dangerous for companies that generate revenues in rubles but incur expenses in another currency, such as US dollars. They are then exposed to open currency risk and such days as we saw yesterday or today are very painful to them," she said.

Companies could hedge themselves against such a depreciation of the ruble, but not all of them did so, Geciauskiene said.

"It was possible to hedge against the ruble's fall, but a considerable part of businesses failed to do so and they see what they see today: a decline in the value of their revenues," she told BNS.

Vilnius newsroom, verslas@bns.lt, +370 5 205 8521

SE News
HD Investors 'must seek Danske refund soon'
BY Charlie Weston
WC 300 words
PD 17 December 2014
SN Irish Independent
SC IINM
ED 1; National
PG 23
LA English
CY (c) 2014 Independent Newspapers Ireland Ltd

LP 

SMALL-TIME property investors have been warned they have just months to get refunds from Danske Bank after the lender lost a string of cases about rates being charged on buy-to-let mortgages.

The bank lost a number of cases before the Financial Services Ombudsman after moving buy-to-let investors onto higher mortgage interest rates.

TD 

Danske Bank was forced to refund anyone who complained, but the ombudsman did not tell the bank to apply a blanket refund.

Founder of Askaboutmoney.com Brendan Burgess said: "Time is running out for people who want to seek a refund, as the incident first started in February 2009 - six years will be up next February."

The six-year rule precludes the ombudsman from dealing with cases that date back more than six years. Danske Bank, which has since closed its retail operation here, yesterday said that it has complied fully with the direction of the ombudsman on the matter.

Many investors who complained at the time about being moved on to a more expensive variable rate than those with residential mortgages won compensation.

The bank had denied that it had moved to unilaterally change the terms and conditions on buy-to-let mortgages. Danske had originally offered all those who took out a mortgage to buy an investment property or a holiday home what it called a "variable rate home loan", with the rate on this described as the "homeloan rate".

A number of investors said they had decided to take out their investor mortgage with the bank, as it was the only one to offer a home-loan rate, rather than an investor rate for investor properties.

Other lenders were charging a premium of 1pc to 1.5pc for investment-property mortgages.

VILNIUS, Dec 17, BNS - The Lithuanian branch of Danske Bank, Denmark's biggest financial group, has extended a loan of 25.5 million euros to Axis Industries, one of Lithuania's largest industrial and energy project groups.

Axis Industries will use the money to finance the group's projects and for working capital needs, mostly bank guarantee issuance, the bank said in a press release on Wednesday.

LP 

(updates)

VILNIUS, Dec 17, BNS - The Lithuanian branch of Danske Bank, Denmark's biggest financial group, has extended a loan of 25.5 million euros to Axis Industries, one of Lithuania's largest industrial and energy project groups.

TD 

Axis Industries Finance and Administration Director Giedrius Barcys told BNS that the biggest amount of funding will be needed for a large cogeneration power plant project in Estonia, but the group will use the loan to finance other projects as well.

"Danske Bank is our group's main financial partner. It offered the most favorable loan terms in the market," he said.

Estonia's Auragen in November awarded a contract to Axis Technologies, a company of Axis Industries, as the general contractor for the construction and equipment of a 21.4-megawatt biofuel cogeneration power plant in Tallinn. At 65 million euros, this is Axis Industries' largest ever project.

Barcys said that the group has expansion plans in Estonia, but added that potential projects are still in a negotiating stage.

"It is too early to disclose these projects to the public. We have no agreements yet. We are simply talking with several potential customers about possible cooperation," he told BNS.

The bulk of the loan will go toward the group's projects both in Lithuania and in Estonia, Latvia, Sweden and other countries, Barstys said.

Icor held 99.44 percent of shares in Axis Industries at the end of last year.

HD Danske Bank forecasts slight economic slow down for Lithuania
WC 360 words
PD 18 December 2014
SN Lithuanian News Agency - ELTA
SC ELTA
LA English
CY (c) 2014 Lithuanian News Agency - ELTA

LP 

Vilnius, December 18 (ELTA) - Economic growth of 2.9 percent of GDP in Lithuania should be the highest among the Baltic States in 2014. However, in 2015 it is likely to decrease to 2.7 percent, while Estonia's will be 2.3 percent and Latvia's 2.9 percent, forecasts Danske Bank.

According to the bank, the motor of Lithuania's economic growth in 2015 will be domestic demand as consumers seem to be spending more. Export is likely to grow gradually, but is expected to fully recover only in 2016.

TD 

Rokas Grajauskas, Baltic Analyst of Danske Bank, says export was the main factor responsible for the slowdown of economy in 2014. Export is likely to insignificantly decline for the first time after 2009. The main reason behind this is the 27 percent of decrease in oil product sales abroad. If oil product export is excluded, Lithuania's total export should grow by around 6 percent.

Danske Bank forecasts that Lithuania's GDP growth in 2015 will be the lowest throughout 2013-2016. In 2013 Lithuania's GDP growth was at 3.3 percent, in 2014 it is expected to slow down to 2.9 percent, while in 2015 to 2.7 percent, but in 2016 it should increase to 3.1 percent.

The bank predicts that geopolitical tensions with Russia will be the determining factor for export and domestic markets of the Baltic States. According to Grajauskas in September-October dairy and meat product export from Lithuania to Belarus jumped up dozens of times. Meanwhile, after Russia imposed an embargo on certain products, their export to other countries has been growing consistently. Although it is often said that from 1 to 3 years are needed to find new markets, but Lithuanian businessmen have once again demonstrated their flexibility. Their products are sold not only in the European Union, but in the United States, Saudi Arabia, Egypt and the South East Asia. Nonetheless, the bank states that Lithuanian economy has not taken the full advantage of such markets as China, the Middle East or the South East Asia.

Karolis Broga

HD Dollar festive hangover to be shortlived
BY Michael Hunter
WC 252 words
PD 22 December 2014
ET 09:14
SN Financial Times (FT.Com)
SC FTCMA
LA English
CY Copyright 2014 The Financial Times Ltd. All rights reserved. Please do not cut and paste FT articles and redistribute by email or post to the web.

LP 

Could the run-in to 2015 leave dollar bulls with a hangover after the US currency's long, hard party during the current year?

Analysis from Danske Bank on Friday's positioning data from the Commodities and Futures Trading Commission implies that the US currency could cause a few headaches toward the new year.

TD 

It reveals that traders moving to cover short positions in the Swiss franc, the yen and sterling cut their aggregate dollar-exposure for the third consecutive week, by $7.4bn - the largest reduction during a week in nine months.

"We emphasise that the dollar is highly vulnerable to temporary corrections," said Kristoffer Kjr Lomholt, Danske analyst.

"This is the case as speculative long-dollar accounts remain stretched, thereby exposing the greenback to profit-taking when the relief rally in risk assets wanes . . . The reduced appetite for the dollar reflects profit-taking and risk reduction ahead of the year end."

Overall, 2014 has been a year strong for the dollar. Even after factoring in the dovish elements of last week's Federal Reserve statement, the dollar index is up 1.5 per cent in December and 10 per cent over the year as a whole.

Danske does not expect the pressure on the US currency to last, saying it expects the dollar to "strengthen" during the first half of 2015.

"We still think the dollar fundamentally looks attractive, even after the recent appreciation," concludes the bank.

michael.hunter@ft.com

OSLO, Jan 6 (Reuters) - The Norwegian purchasing managers' index (PMI) fell to 49.8 points on a seasonally adjusted basis in December from an upwardly revised 51.4 in November, data from logistics association NIMA and Danske Bank showed on Tuesday.

The employment subindicator fell to its lowest level since June 2012, indicating that the most recent drop in oil prices has triggered a fresh round of job cuts in oil related industries, NIMA and Danske Bank said in a statement.

CY (c) 2015 Baltic News Service

LP 

VILNIUS, Jan 06, BNS - Danske Bank, one of the biggest banks in Scandinavia and Western Europe, forecasts that Lithuania's average unemployment level will ease to 10.5 percent this year, from an estimated 10.8 percent in 2014, and will edge further down to 10.2 percent next year.

"Although the Lithuanian economy has grown quite rapidly in recent years, the rate of decline in unemployment is decelerating. The key reasons behind this are a lack of flexibility in labor relations regulation and a too-high minimum wage level," the bank said in a press release on Tuesday.

TD 

Latvia's relatively free labor market does not offset high taxes and lower employee productivity. The country's unemployment level is forecast to ease to 10.6 percent this year and to 10.2 percent in 2016, from an estimated 10.9 percent last year, it said.

Danske Bank's analysts forecast that Estonia's labor market will remain the healthiest in the region, with unemployment in the country estimated at 7.7 percent in 2014 and expected to stay at a similar level in 2015 and 2016.

Vilnius newsroom, verslas@bns.lt, +370 5 205 8521

HD Danske Bank expects low oil price to boost Danish growth
WC 217 words
PD 8 January 2015
ET 03:01
SN Reuters News
SC LBA
LA English
CY Copyright 2015 Thomson Reuters. All Rights Reserved.

LP 

COPENHAGEN, Jan 8 (Reuters) - Danske Bank expects the decline in oil prices to boost economic growth in Denmark by between 0.3 and 0.4 percentage points in 2015, the bank said on Thursday.

Oil prices have dropped by 55 percent since last summer, although Danske Bank predicted they would slowly increase in 2015.

TD 

"Tumbling oil prices are also the main impetus behind the upward revision to our growth forecast for this year," the bank's economists wrote in a research note.

Danske Bank raised its growth forecast for 2015 to 1.6 percent from the 1.3 percent it predicted in October. The growth forecast for 2016 is 2.0 percent.

The Danish economy is on the right track, the bank said, noting that 2014 was the first time since 2011 that the country saw growth in all four quarters.

Danske predicted fiscal budget deficits of less than 2.5 percent of GDP for 2015 and 2016, well within the 3 percent limit defined by the European Union's Stability and Growth Pact.

Parliament's 2015 fiscal budget bill, which was recently approved, predicted a deficit of 3 percent of GDP. (Reporting by Ole Mikkelsen, editing by Terje Solsvik)

HD Danske Bank expects falling oil prices to keep inflation in Baltics low
WC 376 words
PD 9 January 2015
ET 07:16
SN Baltic Business Daily
SC BALDAI
LA English
CY (c) 2015 Baltic News Service

LP 

VILNIUS, Jan 09, BNS - Analysts at Danske Bank, one of the biggest banks in Scandinavia and Western Europe, forecast that falling crude oil prices and deflation in the eurozone will remain the key factors keeping inflation in the Baltic countries low.

Danske Bank forecasts that this year annual inflation will rise to 1.3 percent in Lithuania, 1.6 percent in Latvia and 1.7 percent in Estonia. However, it expects that price growth will stay close to zero in the first half of 2015 and will begin to accelerate only at the end of the year.

TD 

"We don't have to look far for the reasons behind low inflation: falling oil prices turned the inflation spiral around even in the period of economic growth in the Baltic countries," Rokas Grajauskas, a Baltic analyst at Danske Bank, said in a press release on Friday.

"2014 saw a decline in prices for most energy resources and products, first of all, oil, but not only: natural gas, automotive fuel, heating and electricity prices have fallen recently too. Overall, energy product prices in 2014 fell by 3.6 percent in Lithuania, by 1.7 percent in Latvia and by 3.9 percent in Estonia," he said.

According to Grajauskas, falling energy prices knocked 0.5-0.8 percentage points off inflation in the Baltic countries. Without the energy resource price decline, the rate of inflation last year would have been 1 percent in Lithuania, 1.2 percent in Latvia and 1.3 percent in Estonia.

"The price of oil is likely to fall slightly further in the first half of the year and approach 40 US dollars per barrel. Lingering low oil prices may force economists to revise this year's inflation forecast," he said.

Statistics Lithuania earlier in the day released data showing Lithuania's average annual inflation rate in 2014 at 0.1 percent. Estonia registered 0.4 percent inflation. Latvia posted 0.7 percent inflation for January through November

Danske Bank forecasts that next year inflation will reach 2 percent in Lithuania, 2.1 percent in Estonia and 2.3 percent in Latvia.

Vilnius newsroom, verslas@bns.lt, +370 5 205 8520

HD Rouble 'set to touch new lows'
BY Bloomberg
WC 654 words
PD 13 January 2015
SN China Daily
SC CHNDLY
PG 18
LA English
CY Copyright 2015 China Daily Information Company. All rights reserved.

LP 

Ratings agencies say economic outlook worsens amid Ukraine conflict, oil fall

The world's top rouble forecaster is unimpressed by the currency's 30 percent rebound from a record low.

TD 

The analyst - Danske Bank A/S's Vladimir Miklashevsky - said that the rouble may be testing new lows again this quarter as the plunge in oil, Russia's top export, threatens to cost the country its investment-grade credit ratings and turns Russians away from their currency.

The rouble traded at 61.55 per dollar on Friday, after reaching 80.1 on Dec 16, the weakest on record.

"We can easily see records as the oil price is much lower," said Miklashevsky from Brondby, Denmark.

Concern over a rating cut and the loss of confidence among Russians "are the ingredients for a further bout of weakness," he said.

Depreciation would exacerbate the challenges facing President Vladimir Putin as the economy teeters on the edge of a recession and investors dump the nation's bonds.

Fitch Ratings downgraded Russian debt on Friday to the lowest investment grade amid plummeting crude prices and sanctions over Ukraine, maintaining a negative outlook.

Standard & Poor's is also weighing a junk rating for the world's biggest energy exporter.

Russia's economic outlook has "deteriorated significantly since mid-2014" after the sharp falls in the oil price and the rouble, coupled with a steep rise in local interest rates, Fitch said in its statement.

The nation's rouble notes lost 55 percent in dollar terms since the end of June, the biggest decline in the Bloomberg Emerging Market Local Sovereign Index.

Danske, which topped Bloomberg's rankings of foreign-exchange analysts for the four quarters through December, predicts the rouble will average 75 to 77 a dollar in the first quarter.

Options information compiled by Bloomberg shows a 35 percent probability of the currency setting a new all-time low by March 31.

Brent crude is trading almost $10 below the $60 per barrel level that the Russian central bank has said could lead to the economy shrinking as much as 4.7 percent this year.

Sanctions related to the Ukraine conflict have shut Russian companies out of global capital markets.

The rouble has lost 8.3 percent just since the start of the year - after a 46 percent slide in 2014.

While S&P signaled last month it may drop Russia below investment grade within 90 days, traders of credit default swaps already treat the nation as junk.

If S&P does downgrade Russia, all of the country's assets will feel the pain, said Tatiana Orlova, chief economist for Russia at Royal Bank of Scotland Group Plc in London.

It may have a contagion effect on other markets, the second-most accurate forecaster said.

RBS, which last month predicted the rouble at 55 to the dollar in the first quarter, is reviewing that prediction and will not exclude further weakness, Orlova said.

She does not expect the central bank to sell dollars or raise interest rates further. Instead, the government may put pressure on exporters to sell their foreign-exchange holdings.

The yield on the government's rouble-denominated notes due in August 2023 jumped to 16.2 percent on Friday from 8.38 percent at the end of June.

Not everyone is lowering their rouble outlook.

HSBC Holdings Plc, the third most-accurate rouble forecaster in the rankings, is keeping its quarter-end prediction at 59.30.

"The situation in the oil market is very fluid and we have yet to see the full impact of the recent central bank and government measures on the rouble," said Murat Toprak, an HSBC strategist in London.

While the rouble may weaken to about 65 per dollar, it will then appreciate gradually, RBC Capital Markets analysts Daniel Tenengauzer and Daria Parkhomenko wrote in a note to clients on Thursday.

HD Danske Bank setting up IT services center in Vilnius
WC 181 words
PD 14 January 2015
ET 07:43
SN Baltic Business Daily
SC BALDAI
LA English

LP 

VILNIUS, Jan 14, BNS - Danske Bank, one of the biggest banks in Scandinavia and Western Europe, is setting up an IT services center, Danske Group IT Lietuva, in Vilnius.

The new unit would be led by Giedrius Dzekunskas, former head of Barclays IT center in Lithuania, Invest Lithuania, the governmental FDI promotion agency, said in a press release on Wednesday.

TD 

We will create functions responsible for IT services instead of individual jobs. In areas with the critical mass of IT employees, we will also look for managers who will be fully responsible for the creation and development of specific IT services across the group of Danske Bank, the press release quoted Dzekunskas as saying.

According to Justinas Pagirys, director of the Investment Development Department at Invest Lithuania, Danske Bank would join the top three of the biggest investors in Lithuania, alongside the services centers operated by Barclays and Western Union.

Danske Bank runs similar IT services centers in Denmark and India.

HD Danske Bank to open IT service centre in Vilnius
WC 345 words
PD 14 January 2015
SN Lithuanian News Agency - ELTA
SC ELTA
LA English
CY (c) 2015 Lithuanian News Agency - ELTA

LP 

Vilnius, January 14 (ELTA) - Danske Bank, the largest financial services group in Denmark and the second largest in terms of assets owned in Northern Europe, is establishing an IT service centre for its group of companies, Danske Group IT Lietuva (DGITL), in Vilnius, Invest Lithuania said.

Giedrius Dzekunskas has been appointed manager of the group's new IT centre. Earlier he was the manager of the Barclays technology centre in Lithuania. The DGITL centre in Vilnius will contribute to the centres that are already operating in Denmark and India.

TD 

"The fact that the group decided to further expand its activities in Lithuania is really gratifying. It means that we are trusted and this is beneficial to the economy of the entire country," Gintautas Galvanauskas, manager of Danske Bank in Lithuania, said. According to Galvanauskas, the Danske Bank group finds it important to be in an area where there are many talented in the field of IT. This helps develop and implement IT solutions leading to successful competition in the world of electronic banking.

The head of the new division, Dzekunskas, notes that the group's decision to expand its activities in Lithuania is also a high evaluation of Lithuanian IT specialists. The decision to establish a new division was made following the assessment of the IT industry in Lithuania and of the fact that the market has especially highly qualified IT specialists.

"We will create not separate jobs, but functions, responsible for IT services. When there is a critical mass of IT staff, we will look for managers, fully responsible for the implementation and development of specific IT services in all Danske Bank Group," says manager of DGITL G. Dzekunskas. "Considering our growth plans, this is a big responsibility and challenge for maturity of Lithuanian IT community: both professionals and leaders. Therefore, from the first year we will also invest in education and training of IT talents. This year we will start with the program for 10 graduates and will actively cooperate with universities".

Irma Janiauskait

HD Danske Bank forecloses on Ely bar outlet
BY Sarah McCabe
WC 428 words
PD 19 January 2015
SN Irish Independent
SC IINM
ED 1; National
PG 1
LA English
CY (c) 2015 Independent Newspapers Ireland Ltd

LP 

POPULAR Irish bar chain Ely has been forced to close a profitable outlet after failing to reach a deal with exiting lender Danske Bank on a property loan.

Danske foreclosed on loans attached to a property owned by restaurant and bar chain Ely, amid its speedy exit from the Irish market.

TD 

Erik Robson, a director of Ely, said he believed the bank was unwilling to work with the company to restructure the loan.

Celebrity-favourite Ely had fallen into arrears on the property loan, though the business it was operating at the site was profitable. The loan was borrowed from National Irish Bank, the former name of Danske Bank.

As a result the company closed its business in the fashionable Dublin district Grand Canal Dock yesterday, the busiest of all its outlets.

The property has been bought by the Kylemore Group for 4.8m. Property prices have recovered significantly in the Dublin docklands area over the last 12 months.

Kylemore intends to open a restaurant at the venue. All of Ely Grand Canal's 50 staff will be kept on for the new business.

"Ely restaurant group wishes to thank their loyal supporters, neighbours, suppliers, distinguished press and valued customers for their continued commitment," the company said in a statement.

"Most importantly, they are sincerely grateful to the entire dedicated staff of Ely gastro bar. Staff members have been kept informed and Ely has ensured that no jobs have been lost".

Selling the property and securing the jobs was the best result in the circumstances, Mr Robson said.

The company decided that competing with other bidders to buy the property once again was too expensive an option. S

Denmark's Danske Bank announced it was exiting retail banking and most business banking in the Republic of Ireland following years of losses. It will retain a small specialist bank based in Dublin, servicing large corporate clients.

The announcement of its exit came weeks after a similar move by ACC Bank, the Irish subsidiary of Dutch lender Rabobank. Loan-servicing company Pepper has taken over responsibility for the day-to-day running of many of Danske's outstanding Irish loans and mortgages. Personal banking customers were forced to move to other lenders.

Reports also suggest the lender is planning to sell 500m worth of small business loans.

In numbers 15,000 The number of current account customers Danske had when it started closing accounts early last year 1.5bn The profit its Denmark parent made from core activities in 2013
